    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer10637643684794885348">Apparently, just around the bend is everything we’ve been looking forward to including world peace, winning the lottery and a blissful retirement. Perhaps we’re too busy with the r</span>
  <span id="freeText10637643684794885348" style="display:none">Apparently, just around the bend is everything we’ve been looking forward to including world peace, winning the lottery and a blissful retirement. Regrettably, the energy and drive most of us need to enjoy them, should they materialise, have been left way behind us. The buzz word is ‘Now’ but somehow we always seem to be either side of it. Perhaps we’re too busy with the rituals of daily life to consider what homilies like ‘Know Thyself’, and ‘Who am I?’ really mean. Maybe we missed something along the way, or prefer to live with the mystery of it all - contenting ourselves with ‘poster’ philosophy. However, if ‘poster’ philosophy leaves you feeling dissatisfied, then this book, which covers a range of mind-stretching topics, might be just what you’re looking for.</span>

            if ($('edition_23117945').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_23117945').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

</script></div>

<div id="review_1923955807" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1923955807" />
    <a title="Mischenko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko"><img alt="Mischenko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587209348p2/1194517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1923955807?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mischenko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mischenko" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko">Mischenko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1923955807" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17092334357026429110">To see this review and others please visit <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.readrantrockandroll.com'>www.readrantrockandroll.com</a><br/><br/><i>Just Around the Bend</i> by Renée Paule is a book about letting go of the past and living in the now. <br/><br/>I was forewarned ahead of time that Renée Paule's books make you feel like you're looking into a mirror. As I continued reading, this became a reality for me. I was pulled into the book and couldn't put it down. There were many "Aha" moments for me. I also felt a direct connection to some of the author's experiences and feel I've </span>
  <span id="freeText17092334357026429110" style="display:none">To see this review and others please visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.readrantrockandroll.com">www.readrantrockandroll.com</a><br /><br /><i>Just Around the Bend</i> by Renée Paule is a book about letting go of the past and living in the now. <br /><br />I was forewarned ahead of time that Renée Paule's books make you feel like you're looking into a mirror. As I continued reading, this became a reality for me. I was pulled into the book and couldn't put it down. There were many "Aha" moments for me. I also felt a direct connection to some of the author's experiences and feel I've made many mistakes because this is something I haven't truly gotten over and accepted. It's amazing these pent up emotions we hold on to inside and don't even realize it. <br /><br />What I loved especially about the book was that the author speaks as if this is something we are experiencing together by using the word "we." It's not like someone telling <i>you</i> what you're doing wrong, but more of an observation on how <i>we</i> as humans handle our emotions and how <i>we</i> should realize that we're the ones in control. We can change everything. We're on a journey together. What are we feeling, why, and how are we supposed to react? This book won't give you answers or instructions like a self-help book on how you can fix yourself, but will give you the insight and awareness needed to guide you in the right direction to stop this cycle of thinking and behavior.<br /><br />Here's something long forgotten by many people in this world-<b>humanity is a team.</b> Whether we like it or not, we work together. On the section titled, "Independence" the author discusses this fact. I recently heard a radio broadcast on NPR regarding the <b>lack of compassion</b> that people have for one another. This is a huge issue, isn't it? There could be a massive fight going on with someone getting beaten badly somewhere and rather than call 911, people are getting on their cell phones and recording it so they can upload it to YouTube later when they get home, or post it on Facebook. This is horrible. When we start separating ourselves from each others, problems arise. When we stop thinking about humanity and lose compassion for others, we go backwards. <br /><br />In the section "Humanity is One" the author discusses humans and how we're wonderfully made. One of my favorite quotes from this section,<i>"The world has many problems and many unhappy people living in it, but we don't have to be that way to. No matter how miserable we feel we ought to become or how guilty we feel about being happy whilst others are suffering, we won't make the world a better place to live in. We can only make the world happier by being happier in it; every move counts and the more people make them, the better.</i>-Renée Paule<br /><br /><i>“We're humanity and no matter how individual or superior we think we are, we're part of a greater whole. We can't find completeness somewhere else any more than an individual part of a one-thousand-piece jigsaw puzzle can. We all belong together and we always will. When we hurt each other what we're really doing is hurting ourself and damaging the world in which we all must live.” </i> -Renée Paule<br /><br /><i>“Imagine living in a world where we no longer believe that war can lead to peace. War can't lead to peace anymore than ignorance can lead to knowledge. War leads to premature death, pain, suffering, hatred, fear and more separation.” </i>-Renée Paule<br /><br />My favorite sections included: A Bit of a Rant, Completeness, Independence, What If and Other Worries, and Attachment. The simple (Dilly) illustrations make very powerful statements alone. <br /><br /><b>I think everyone could take something from this book and hope more will read it. It's not a self-help book at all, so please don't be afraid to read it if you're one of those people afraid of those types of books. This isn't it. This is the author's journey and at the same time a call to humanity.</b><br /><br />I'm looking forward to reading more from this author and feel lucky to have met her. I'd like to thank Renée Paule for sending me a complimentary copy. Now, back to the first book! <br /><br />5*****</span>

<div id="review_2346965718" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2346965718" />
    <a title="Amalia Gkavea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56789747-amalia-gkavea"><img alt="Amalia Gkavea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559158764p2/56789747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2346965718?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amalia Gkavea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amalia Gkavea" href="/user/show/56789747-amalia-gkavea">Amalia Gkavea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=psychology-mentality">psychology-mentality</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=sociology">sociology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2346965718" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16188879386350121084"><i>
  <b>‘’We speak sweet intentions but our hearts remain silent.’’</b>
</i><br/><br/><i>Just Around the Bend</i> was the only book by Renée Paule that I hadn’t read and it ended up being my favourite. I love her work, I find that in every book of hers her words speak to me and in <i>Just Around the Bend</i> I found chapters that made me contemplate (once more) on one of the banes of our existence. The Past and its steadfast roots in our lives.<br/><br/>Please, don’t get me wrong. I love the Past. It is what defines us, it makes us who we ar</span>
  <span id="freeText16188879386350121084" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>‘’We speak sweet intentions but our hearts remain silent.’’</b>
</i><br /><br /><i>Just Around the Bend</i> was the only book by Renée Paule that I hadn’t read and it ended up being my favourite. I love her work, I find that in every book of hers her words speak to me and in <i>Just Around the Bend</i> I found chapters that made me contemplate (once more) on one of the banes of our existence. The Past and its steadfast roots in our lives.<br /><br />Please, don’t get me wrong. I love the Past. It is what defines us, it makes us who we are as people, as citizens of our countries, of the world we have created for better or for worse. However, it can also become a strict, ever-watchful warden. It can keep us chained to wrong choices, decisions that were never taken and a thousand ‘’what ifs’’ that lead nowhere. I plead guilty to the crime and this is why this book resonated with me to such a degree. I could see myself reflected in the brilliant chapter ‘’Mind Dramas’’ dedicated to the various ways our mind works to keep us glued to the Past. How we spend our lives acting out all the different scenarios in our heads of what may be and, most importantly, what could have been. We all fall into that trap and there is no easy way out.<br /><br />Another subject that was all to familiar had to do with the social media and the way exposure influences the interactions and relationships in our lives. I understand that we’re all exposed. Of course, the degree varies but even writing a small review is a way of disclosing thoughts and feelings to people we don’t know, people we’ll probably never meet in real life. Our writing uncovers our ways of viewing life and a good or a bad book may even influence our momentary behaviour. Now, I don’t have a Facebook page but even if I had, I’d never accept real life friends. A fraction between two of our friends may cause a fraction in our lives and who needs more drama that has nothing to do with us? We face enough challenges on a daily basis, I don’t think we need an online ordeal as well. Same goes for the various trolls who comment on our posts and reviews, presuming to know everything better than the reviewer. Those people are in dire need of a thing called ‘’life’’ and, incidentally, I can’t even begin to tell you the peace of mind I acquired once I activated the ‘’no comments from non-friends’’ option on Goodreads…<br /><br />As always, Renée poses the questions in clear, direct and sincere language and doesn’t give us the answers. She provides the material for the readers to think and try to decide. Her books aren’t detrimental ‘’self-help’’ pseudo-manuals but stops on our way to the effort of understanding ourselves and our surroundings. I don’t know what could be more realistically useful than that.<br /><br />Many thanks to Renée for the opportunity to find a small path towards a healthier way of looking upon certain issues that have weighted me down for too long…<br /><br />My reviews can also be found on <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://theopinionatedreaderblog.wordpress.com">https://theopinionatedreaderblog.word...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16188879386350121084" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1954090542" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1954090542" />
    <a title="Brian Michels" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53247692-brian-michels"><img alt="Brian Michels" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458452341p2/53247692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1954090542?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brian Michels" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brian Michels" href="/user/show/53247692-brian-michels">Brian Michels</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1954090542" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2604225491273592602">What is a book review?<br/><br/>Wikipedia defines it as:<br/><br/>…a form of literary criticism in which a book is analyzed based on content, style, and merit. A book review may be a primary source, opinion piece, summary review or scholarly review. ... A book review's length may vary from a single paragraph to a substantial essay.<br/><br/>That’s a decent description, especially coming from a porn producer (Wikipedia’s Steven Hirsch and Vivid Entertainment: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PXYkVw3tpH4'>https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PXYkV...</a> ) as opposed to a refined </span>
  <span id="freeText2604225491273592602" style="display:none">What is a book review?<br /><br />Wikipedia defines it as:<br /><br />…a form of literary criticism in which a book is analyzed based on content, style, and merit. A book review may be a primary source, opinion piece, summary review or scholarly review. ... A book review's length may vary from a single paragraph to a substantial essay.<br /><br />That’s a decent description, especially coming from a porn producer (Wikipedia’s Steven Hirsch and Vivid Entertainment: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PXYkVw3tpH4">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PXYkV...</a> ) as opposed to a refined Scholars Guild or a learned book club. What I’m trying to highlight is that a review, whether a deep analyzation or a simple thumb-up, no matter what walk of life it comes from, boils down to a simple dish of subjectivity. Some dishes are more popular or more respected than others. But in absolute terms, a dish is a dish and a dish is a dish, and like a pie hole, everyone has got one.<br /><br />I explain this because Just Around The Bend is a book that many, many people will overwhelmingly enjoy, while others will not care for it in the least. More to my point, Just Around The Bend is heavy with subjectivity.<br /><br />So, what’s my dish on the book?<br /><br />There’s a big portion of good and few dabs of bad. (Reminder, this review is hinged to my subjectivity.)<br /><br /><br />First, the good:<br /><br />The best thing, Renee’s voice is irresistible. She possesses that rare talent that distinguishes a great writer from the rest: a natural ability to captivate. It is a gentle yet courageous voice. A voice worthy of leadership. A voice filled with serious life experience and thirsty for more, and with an undeniable desire to share the joys and struggles of all of it. Most importantly, it is a voice that resonates when truth is spoken, like a beautiful singer. That is enough to make the book shine but there’s more.<br /><br />If you normally float around on the shallow side of the pool and you’re curious about deeper waters, Just Around The Bend has plenty of insight and encouragement to spare, enough to soak your head well and good. If you are firmly planted, stuck, on the shallow end and perhaps fret dense philosophical tomes on human thought, keep your cool because Rene’s writing style is incredibly plain and simple, like comfortable Lead slippers that will gently coax you to the greatest depths of it all. The narration is akin to a great conversation with a loving and wise old friend. Need more? Perhaps the simple notion of words get you flustered and shuts you down. Don’t sweat it, Renee has you covered, incorporated throughout the book is a series of illustrations (drawn by the author) helping you along with a number of complex human conundrums. There’s more, a number of unexpected reflections. I particularly liked her contrarian assessment of institutional education and how ridiculous it has become. Also, her evaluation and advise on peer pressure can be stacked along with the best of them. <br /><br /><br />Now, a few dabs of bad:<br /><br />(Note: the number of words in my review are not dished out proportionally correct between impressive good points and the 3 small points I had issue with. This imbalance might lead to misinterpreting my review in a lesser light than I tried to convey. Just Around The Bend is a great book and easily warrants my 4 Star rating.)<br /><br />1 - Vibrations (in the context of spirituality or other-worldly experiences). I’ve been hearing about Vibrations (or “frequencies”) here and there from all sorts over the years, enough to have me consider it a quasi religion loosely feathered with Hinduism, Buddhism, Sufism, and all new-age exoticisms. I don’t meditate with any of those systems. Still, I do understand the concept of Vibrations. In fact, I have a built-in daily reminder: the giant boiler room beneath my apartment directly below the seat I sit in as I write this review; it vibrates constantly - and not at all in that Hammacher Schlemmer desirable way or with a hint of spiritualism. The problem I have with the shaky religion (Vibrations) is that it is so abstract that it loses potency and relativity to and for a practical life; it comes up vague and hollow while trying to get something tangible out of a mystical belief system; it keeps one’s focus far out in a forever-grasping mode in an attempt to be hyper sensitive to spiritual vibrations when the world of necessity and practical compassion is at the tip of your nose. Vibrations is the proverbial carrot dangling (or vibrating) from a stick out in front of the horse. With it as your foundational belief, you’ll only have sustained yearning, no filled heart. I think there is a time for seeking answers to unanswerable question and then it’s time to take what you’ve learned and live with it, (of course while maintaining an open mind to possibilities). Vibrations appear somewhat pointless in connecting with others. Their words, actions, and a deep look into their eyes delivers all the connectivity I need. Connecting to the greatness of it all, the infinite, the universe, God, for me, it doesn’t vibrate - it’s a full blown symphony. Note: a friendly reminder about my subjectivity.<br /><br />2 - Oneness (or We Are The World). Whoa! Low-life, two-bit criminals and thugs, perverts, psychopaths, Luciferians/Satanists, War Criminals of past and present responsible for the death of hundreds of millions of innocent lives are a very real part of the world. I am not One with any of them. Diversity is king in my book. That means I view reality as made up with different types of people with different lifestyles, beliefs and intentions, both good and bad. Many-ness probably better suits me. Oneness is at the core of Just Around The Bend. Make no mistake, Renee’s Oneness is not all bad. In fact it conjures up some of the great commonalities with a blessed understanding; pain; suffering; loneliness; sorrow; etc…<br /><br />3 - Self-Help Book. Our porn producer friend at Wikipedia helps again by explaining that “a self-help book is one that is written with the intention to instruct its readers on solving personal problems.” To be fair, Renee tries to separate herself from the genre of Self-Help by stating: “The author of a self-help book, more often than not, tells us how they found their way and this is not necessarily the right way for us; which is why the effects don’t last.” Is Just Around The Bend truly that different with its goal? Semantics? Renee’s book honestly comes across as out of the ordinary. Categorizing it as Self-Help is not exactly correct. It’s tough for me to define. I’m more in tune with hard knocks and getting up on your own before someone stomps on your head. Someone else’s book about self help is too ironic for me to comprehend. I do not read them.<br /><br />(Note: Recently, I reviewed Nathan Hill’s THE NIX. The book carried a political agenda not anywhere close to what I stand for. I gave the book 5 Stars and a stellar review because the writing style and storyline satisfaction was overwhelmingly great. I try to judge on gratification and merit of craft, not by how closely a book stays in line with my belief system. Of course this is not an absolute. I cannot imagine ever raving about a book that glorifies murder for the sake of murder - even if it was written by the most talented writer in the universe.)<br /><br /><br />Bottom line: if the human condition and life experience are topics that interest you this book will satisfy. Without a doubt it will get even the the best belly button gazers thinking about something new. Because of that quality, I was engaged from cover to cover. Furthermore, this book is a serious serving of inspiration for anyone struggling to face up to whatever may be suppressing or challenging them in their lives. To use a dangerous pronoun, “We” could all use a little help sometimes.<br /><br />Lastly, the old salt head, Plato, famously stated, "An unexamined life is not worth living.” So, it’s simple, get this book if you want to get on with living. In the very least, you will absolutely enjoy listening to Renee. Her challenging life experience has shaped a voice not to be missed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2604225491273592602" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14841937876992824727">I can't believe I have yet to review this one. I was leaving town for a few weeks and this one got lost in the shuffle. Anyway, on to the book. I also had to think about this one. How do I classify it? It's not a self-help book. It's a more of a (I think) wake up to reality and what is going on around you. Take a look and evaluate things, *really* look at everything. Let me say..I'm a weirdo. When I have a book, it must remain pristine. No writing, watermarks, dog-ears, etc. I read it and either</span>
  <span id="freeText14841937876992824727" style="display:none">I can't believe I have yet to review this one. I was leaving town for a few weeks and this one got lost in the shuffle. Anyway, on to the book. I also had to think about this one. How do I classify it? It's not a self-help book. It's a more of a (I think) wake up to reality and what is going on around you. Take a look and evaluate things, *really* look at everything. Let me say..I'm a weirdo. When I have a book, it must remain pristine. No writing, watermarks, dog-ears, etc. I read it and either pass it on to another to enjoy, or I save it to re-read. But with this one, I just could not stop myself....I had to underline passages. There were so many sentences that made me think, go back and read them again. Read a few pages ahead and go back. I had to start marking them. One of my first was 'Humanity can be so childish and immature'. (See recent politics)<br /><br />There are numerous chapters such as Independence, Faith, Attachment, Completeness, and others. But my personal favorite was Mind Dramas. It starts 'Yesterday has already happened - we don't have to remaster, splice, edit or relive it'. Oh but we do and I know I invest way too much of my precious time doing this. And there was What If's and Other Worries - yes, I worry over *everything*. I could read more books if I spent less time thinking and worrying over things, many of which I can't control. Perhaps, be a little bit more easy going.<br /><br />I have to say I won this book after reading a wonderful interview with Mischenko and the author on Mischenko's blog. I was so excited to win this one and read it. It came with a lovely bookmark, which I'm using in other books now. This does not influence my review. :-) I'm so glad to have come across this gem of a book that really helped me *think*. Thanks to the author for sending me this book from Europe.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12536074638504245579">There's a lot of inspiration stuffed inside this little book, and it's definitely one that everybody should read. Illustrated with "Dilly" (a thought form) who accompanies readers as they go through the book, <i>Just Around the Bend</i> is a powerful and impressive guide to life and study of the human experience. The great thing about it is that anybody can read it. It has no target age range, so either adults or kids can read it and enjoy it and learn from it. There are numerous books on humanity and </span>
  <span id="freeText12536074638504245579" style="display:none">There's a lot of inspiration stuffed inside this little book, and it's definitely one that everybody should read. Illustrated with "Dilly" (a thought form) who accompanies readers as they go through the book, <i>Just Around the Bend</i> is a powerful and impressive guide to life and study of the human experience. The great thing about it is that anybody can read it. It has no target age range, so either adults or kids can read it and enjoy it and learn from it. There are numerous books on humanity and philosophy out there, but <i>Just Around the Bend</i> is so entirely unique that it's in a class all its own. My favourite part of it was definitely the illustrations, which not only provide a touch of the author's originality, but they also display various points being made in the text. This book is amazing and definitely worth reading.</span>

<div id="review_1025411645" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1025411645" />
    <a title="Aleena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32189188-aleena"><img alt="Aleena" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1025411645?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aleena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aleena" href="/user/show/32189188-aleena">Aleena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1025411645" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer112733582915536504">I was honoured to be asked to beta read ‘Just Around the Bend’ as I thoroughly enjoyed Renée’s previous book ‘On the Other Hand’. Having read the book from cover to cover, I came to a realisation that the author has once again timelessly inspired me. I enjoyed every minute of it. And most of all, I loved Dilly. The thought bubble depicted life and how people behave toward each other, and thus show the reader how to look behind what eyes can see. How to think beyond what the mind thinks… I have l</span>
  <span id="freeText112733582915536504" style="display:none">I was honoured to be asked to beta read ‘Just Around the Bend’ as I thoroughly enjoyed Renée’s previous book ‘On the Other Hand’. Having read the book from cover to cover, I came to a realisation that the author has once again timelessly inspired me. I enjoyed every minute of it. And most of all, I loved Dilly. The thought bubble depicted life and how people behave toward each other, and thus show the reader how to look behind what eyes can see. How to think beyond what the mind thinks… I have loved reading it and will dive in it again in order to improve my quality of life inside of me.<br />The book resonated with me and I felt it was written about me, for me. Simple and clear, the author has shared insights that can be applied to life quite easily. While reading the book I realised something - I have to be kinder to me, and should put an end to the interference of all the negative energies that drag me down. I have to embrace life, I have to embrace myself, be true to myself and to live life to the fullest.<br />I have loved reading every word written in this book, as it opened my eyes and helped me observe every thought and every motive behind a human’s action. I found a lot of things in this book that I knew but never actually knew I knew them. But now with a new approach to life, I find it easy to help myself become complete within me. I have stopped looking for external crutches and the illusions of finding happiness through other people. I’m finding it within me and I will cherish it for life, however long or short my life is.<br />I highly recommend this book to anyone who wishes to get a better understanding of their live and live a happier one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="112733582915536504" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1035931104" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3876805463656484844">First of all, as with the author’s first book ‘On The Other Hand’ I declare an interest in ‘Just Around The Bend’. I know the author very well and I edited both books for her. I have not and will not be paid for my services in any way. This book stands on its own merit and needs no props or bias. It’s from this standpoint that I am pleased to write my review.<br/>Written from the viewpoint of an observer ‘Just Around The Bend’ examines the mind of Humanity, the concept of Oneness and the human experi</span>
  <span id="freeText3876805463656484844" style="display:none">First of all, as with the author’s first book ‘On The Other Hand’ I declare an interest in ‘Just Around The Bend’. I know the author very well and I edited both books for her. I have not and will not be paid for my services in any way. This book stands on its own merit and needs no props or bias. It’s from this standpoint that I am pleased to write my review.<br />Written from the viewpoint of an observer ‘Just Around The Bend’ examines the mind of Humanity, the concept of Oneness and the human experience common to all of us; together with all its foibles. Renée Paule has written some unusual essays that, for example, examine what ‘Faith’ is, the ‘Mind Dramas’ we enact and what close ‘Observation’ of our world means. As in her book ‘On The Other Hand’ she does this in her unique conversational, self-reflective and semi-autobiographical style.<br />The book is interesting in that it is both a lens and a mirror; it will have you nodding your head in hearty agreement or shaking it in dissent; which one, I suppose, may depend on whether you catch sight of someone else or yourself. However, there is little, if anything, in this book that can be denied. <br />Just Around the Bend contains some charming illustrations drawn by the author depicting facets of the human psyche discussed within the book. I recommend this book for those of you who are reflecting on their lives or life in general, wondering what it’s all about.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2579588915806510134">Check out the complete review at <a href='https://theverdictsout.wordpress.com/2015/04/01/book-review-of-just-around-the-bend-mas-o-menos-by-renee-paule/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Views She Writes - WordPress Reviews</a><br/><br/>Philosophy has always been my favorite topic. So when I came across this book, there was no second thought. And it was absolutely worth it. Renee has written a beautiful book with so much points to think and ponder about our own life. After reading the book, you really feel like going back and analyzing your life. Renee has given so many points to think of and improve our lives. The book is more of a self help kind of book in a</span>
  <span id="freeText2579588915806510134" style="display:none">Check out the complete review at <a href="https://theverdictsout.wordpress.com/2015/04/01/book-review-of-just-around-the-bend-mas-o-menos-by-renee-paule/" rel="nofollow noopener">Views She Writes - WordPress Reviews</a><br /><br />Philosophy has always been my favorite topic. So when I came across this book, there was no second thought. And it was absolutely worth it. Renee has written a beautiful book with so much points to think and ponder about our own life. After reading the book, you really feel like going back and analyzing your life. Renee has given so many points to think of and improve our lives. The book is more of a self help kind of book in a very different.<br /><br />There are so many self help books available in the market? So what is different about this one? All the other books give us answers to questions which may not be even relevant to us. Renee with her book “Just around the bend” gives us only questions, but those questions are more useful and beneficial than all the other irrelevant answers. These questions make us think and find answers tailor made for ourselves. These answers which we find out ourselves help us so much better than all the ready made answers we get through other self help books<br /><br />The way she has explained to find happiness within and not to search for someone else to make you happy is something really amazing. Chapters like emotion being energy in motion, or perception, really makes you wonder at things you would never have thought about. The question “Would you be your own friend if you were to meet yourself someday?” is a well known question to check if you find yourself interesting. And Renee has put it up wonderfully in the book.<br /><br />The book is deeply philosophical and insightful. The entire journey with the book had been beautiful and really knowledgeable. Unfortunately I read the second book first and now going to the first book. But after this, I am sure I will love the first book just as much, if not more.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11637606177244610565">My overall impression when I first finished the book was that, although I’d enjoyed it, there was something missing. Consequently I read back through and realised that what I was unconsciously hankering after were answers – exactly what the book set out to avoid! <br/><br/>In places a little more explanation of a line of thought, or concept, could have been helpful and at the other extreme an idea occasionally felt a little ‘over-egged.’ But then that is the beauty of Renée’s book – it really does make yo</span>
  <span id="freeText11637606177244610565" style="display:none">My overall impression when I first finished the book was that, although I’d enjoyed it, there was something missing. Consequently I read back through and realised that what I was unconsciously hankering after were answers – exactly what the book set out to avoid! <br /><br />In places a little more explanation of a line of thought, or concept, could have been helpful and at the other extreme an idea occasionally felt a little ‘over-egged.’ But then that is the beauty of Renée’s book – it really does make you think for yourself without feeding you the answers that are the result of another’s experience. This is a book that underlines the importance of taking control of the self through being aware of one’s thoughts, rather than being a blind slave to them. Of freeing oneself to see what is really happening, both in the individual mind and that of humankind in general. Top marks for being an enjoyable read that's truly about looking at and taking responsibility for the self, rather than being a slick, dumbed-down instructional manual that simply follows another’s path.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11637606177244610565" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText7644833549823290326" style="display:none">*** Note: I received review copy of this book from the author, in exchange for an honest review. I am glad I got a chance to read this book. ***<br /><br />The book has beautiful starting lines with a philosophical poem. First two chapters of the book preface and introduction gave the good idea on what there will be in the book and author’s intention on writing this book and also how it is different than other self-help book.<br /><br />While the previous book by author On the other Hand, that I read this year, told about questioning conditional belief and seeking questions rather than answers, a first step of the journey of self-discovery, Just Around the Bend, is second step in that journey. Again author doesn’t claim to answers questions, but tells about knowing and observing ourselves better and changing ourselves. What we are doing wrong and how we can make it right and ultimately seek ourselves.<br /><br />Loved all the questions in the book and the philosophical poems in last two chapters. Did I tell you I loved voice of author in this book? I liked On The Other Hand and style of author in that book but in this one I just loved author’s voice even more.<br /><br />Author has discussed many topics that are essential to discover ourselves. Through discussion of the very amazing topics like, completeness, mind drama, independence, what ifs, emotions and energy, observation, attachment, faith, intention, and Humanity, author lead us on the self-discovery path. We get the insight of all these topics with detailed narration of what we are doing wrong, we understand some topics very wrongly to begin with, reasons of unhappiness, how to be more observant, and how we can make things right. Also there was discussion about the title of the book ‘Just around the Bend’.<br /><br />Each chapters starts with the beautiful quote related to the topic discussed in the book. I so loved all the quotes that I have to stop my finger from typing all here. All the things were explained in easy language with few examples.<br /><br />Few things I really liked in the book were-<br /><br />About the internet and Social Medias, how it could be both good and bad depending on our choice. About how we live in poising past and uncertain future rather than living in today, Now. Most beautiful topics were fining Completeness in ourselves, freeing from prison of Attachment and what actually Faith is. These three topic really changed my mind.<br /><br />The way completeness was discussed in the book, how even forming relationship just to fill our incompleteness leads to unhappiness and how finding completeness in ourselves and two such people together can form beautiful relationship few other examples likewise was brilliant. I loved reading about Emotions and Energies. “Emotion= Energy in motion.” Did you know emotions are contagious? This topic discussed about how it can affect us and people around us and how we can free our emotions from traps, and how we can understand our emotions and others, learn to surround ourselves with positive ones and let go of the negative ones, can help us towards peace of mind.<br /><br />Another thing I like was about independence. How wrong I was about this word and after reading this chapter I understood no one is truly independent in seeking independence we are doing so many wrong things. We all and even nature is inter-dependent. We need each other to survive, to change the world and it ultimately lead to the topic unity, being the Whole. Everyone is essential like organs in our bodies they need each other to function the whole body and so we do. This was even more elaborated in ‘Humanity is One’ and sealed the deal of understanding humanity. We all are unique, have talents and as one we are complete.<br /><br />This book showed the mirror, the naked truth, the reality of ourselves, of human nature and of society. The problem we are all experiencing with ourselves, how we can start the change with ourselves in order to change society and can work as one in order to be truly independent.<br /><br />Overall, Few things I already knew and believed in it, some were new to me, and some changed my mind. I learned lot from this book. If all self-help books are like this then I think I would like read them. There is something for everyone here. I recommend this book to all of you, I’m you will start loving self-help books like I did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7644833549823290326" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13753828591873755516" style="display:none">I was lucky enough to be one of the beta readers chosen by Renee Paule, so i received the ARC of Just around the bend: Mas o Menos (complete with suggestive illustrations), and for this i would like to thank the author, this gesture is very much appreciated by me.This book helped me to understand better many things from around me and it came in a difficult time of my life when i needed something like this to open my eyes.This book is like small on the outside but so big on the inside, with so many facts about life, about humanity.The most important thing i have learned is that we cannot live in the past, we cannot let painful memories control us, and in the same time there is no future, so no one should surrender to worries, there is only Now, the present time, here.We should live the moment, this is all we have.The author is an expert in explaining why we should not let feelings of negativity control us and our lives.Our mind can be our best friend or our worst enemy, it depends on us whether we want to live in a ”cage” of sadness or just to be free , with our souls relaxed and happy.This book is not about finding solutions to our daily problems, it is about lighting up a path towards understanding humanity, universe and life.We have to be more opened , we have to live , we have to get out from our houses, and not stay all the time in the same environment, where we are continuously bombarded with bad news on tv, where internet keeps us from having a real interaction with other people.Why do we always choose the easy way out, why do we care so much about other people”s opinions on us, why do we enjoy destroying ourselves?!WE have our eyes open, but can we really see?! I rediscovered myself in this book and how to be more confident in myself, what is the best reaction in different situations, how to overcome obstacles in life by first looking at myself, deep within my soul.”Just around the bend” is about choices, about taking the chance to see what is out there in this crazy world and in our restless minds.Read this book because it will help you more than you can imagine and your energy will be restored.Relax, breathe and read:).Thank you Renee Paule</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1886995593684079257">There was probably a point in your existence that you've been asked a very simple question, and that is "what is life?" back then, a 10-year old me would always say, "life is about being happy and being with your family" When asked in high school, without even thinking much, i would say, life is about achieving success, getting a dream job, getting married and have children, which is the usual portrayal of "the perfect life" that the media would have us believe.<br/> <br/>But what really is life?<br/> <br/>Are we m</span>
  <span id="freeText1886995593684079257" style="display:none">There was probably a point in your existence that you've been asked a very simple question, and that is "what is life?" back then, a 10-year old me would always say, "life is about being happy and being with your family" When asked in high school, without even thinking much, i would say, life is about achieving success, getting a dream job, getting married and have children, which is the usual portrayal of "the perfect life" that the media would have us believe.<br /> <br />But what really is life?<br /> <br />Are we merely just robots of the daily grind, being the mechanical drones of jobs we need to do for a living?<br /> <br />Are we living so that we could enjoy Films, games, social media, these inescapable "distractions?"<br /> <br />So... what is life?<br /> <br />Each time I've read a self-help book, often times it would tell us how we should live, spoon-feeding the answers to the big questions of life. Just around the bend however, only gives you questions. It makes you go deep in your roots and analyzing your own life through a series of insightful essays that cater to a wide array of topics ranging from the use of social media to the author's own personal experiences.<br /> <br />Before reading this book, being through a lot of experiences, I find it quite difficult now to define what life is for me, Especially now that I am in a stage in life where I have to make very important decisions. So I am thrilled to have read this book because it gave me a lot of insight an a lot of different perspectives as to how I would tackle the challenges of life.<br /> <br />Countless lessons are to be learned from this book. Simple lessons, yet full of so much substance. One thing that struck me the most is how the author emphasizes the importance of self-awareness. Being able to control yourself, being aware of what's holding us back in living the life we've always worked hard for. Lastly, The combination of words, illustrations and comics(starring Dilly) add to the whole reading experience.<br /> <br />This book is simply beautiful. I will read this again without hesitation.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1633208049611403236">This book is a natural progression from the author's previous work, "On the Other Hand." I found the book to be fascinating and it helped me to see aspects of myself that I did not like and how I could improve myself. The focus of this book is the 'Now', not the 'Past' or the 'Future' but what is happening right here at this moment. The moment we open this book we are invited to go on a journey with the author to learn about ourselves and what holds us back from our dreams and accomplishments. S</span>
  <span id="freeText1633208049611403236" style="display:none">This book is a natural progression from the author's previous work, "On the Other Hand." I found the book to be fascinating and it helped me to see aspects of myself that I did not like and how I could improve myself. The focus of this book is the 'Now', not the 'Past' or the 'Future' but what is happening right here at this moment. The moment we open this book we are invited to go on a journey with the author to learn about ourselves and what holds us back from our dreams and accomplishments. Some of the lessons in this book are that we don't need others approval in order to feel self worth; we don't have to let negative persons or situations in our life rob us of joy and that Humanity can make huge changes for the better if only they, we, decide to make it happen. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2273331537339693101">Renee Paule's second excursion into the literary world has resulted in the wonderful must read ‘Just Around The Bend’. This book draws you into exploring your world from a different perspective, taking you out of your comfort zone and encouraging you to look at the world through newly opened eyes.<br/>From the first page this is a book that becomes increasingly difficult to put down.<br/>I Love ‘Dilly’, brings a smile to my face and injects an element of humour.</span>

  <span id="freeText18147387894939562785" style="display:none">I received an advanced copy of “Just Around The Bend” in return for a review.<br /><br />Are you ready to take a good deep look at yourself and your world? Are you ready to tackle all that the mind disseminates? If so then Renee Paule's "Just Around The Bend" is a must read.<br /><br />A brilliant follow on from her first book "On The Other Hand", it is an uncomplicated, thought provoking and insightful piece of writing. This is one of those rare books you will not want to close as each chapter simply whets your appetite for what comes next. However, each chapter also needs to be digested.<br /><br />I love the illustrations they really bring a smile to your face and are a great way to emphasise salient points.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2392259765" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16845818802738307726">Renée Paule is a fantastic author. This is her second book, and if the first one was a great read, this is even better. In the book, Renée tackles some of the greater questions in life, in a spiritual journey and in handling those thoughts and setbacks you can't avoid in life. Down to earth and with a smile, Renée shows how she has come to think about life, and she shows the way for all who would want to come along. There are no final answers, and there are no stupid questions. I recommend this </span>
  <span id="freeText16845818802738307726" style="display:none">Renée Paule is a fantastic author. This is her second book, and if the first one was a great read, this is even better. In the book, Renée tackles some of the greater questions in life, in a spiritual journey and in handling those thoughts and setbacks you can't avoid in life. Down to earth and with a smile, Renée shows how she has come to think about life, and she shows the way for all who would want to come along. There are no final answers, and there are no stupid questions. I recommend this books to anyone who enjoys deep thought without the solemnness.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16845818802738307726" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7376084.Ren_e_Paule">About Renée Paule</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/7376084.Ren_e_Paule"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1551894100p3/7376084.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/7376084.Ren_e_Paule">Renée Paule
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
255
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11775023341793871937"><b>'Self-reflection', 'Know Thyself' and 'Semi-autobiography'</b><br/><br/>'Top of the morning' from Ireland.<br/><br/>Many years ago I wrote my autobiography - probably more as therapy than anything else - but life continued happening to me and I got to thinking, what good will this story do, isn’t there enough misery in the world without me adding to it? I subsequently burnt the manuscript. It was around that time that I </span>
  <span id="freeText11775023341793871937" style="display:none"><b>'Self-reflection', 'Know Thyself' and 'Semi-autobiography'</b><br /><br />'Top of the morning' from Ireland.<br /><br />Many years ago I wrote my autobiography - probably more as therapy than anything else - but life continued happening to me and I got to thinking, what good will this story do, isn’t there enough misery in the world without me adding to it? I subsequently burnt the manuscript. It was around that time that I began searching for meaning in my life and had a profound experience - a realisation that we’re all connected; we’re One. In my books, I take an honest look at our quirky and often bizarre behaviour in society and challenge the status-quo we accept as unchangeable - questioning and pushing the boundaries we set ourselves, and those that have been set for us. I’m convinced that if we want to change our lives and change our world then we must first change ourselves. I invite you to join me on my journey, questioning the society we call ours and the role we play within it.<br /><br /><u>My Reviews</u><br />I rate/review books that have given me pause for thought. 5 stars = something resonated with me.<br /><br />Author Interviews, Articles and Questionnaires are at:<br /><br /><a href="https://pebbleinthestillwaters.blogspot.ie/2014/07/author-interview-renee-paule-on-other.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Pebble in the Still Waters</a><br /><a href="https://www.smashwords.com/profile/view/reneepaule" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Smashwords</a><br /><a href="https://twogalsandabook.com/2017/04/17/just-around-the-bend-by-renee-paule-interview-giveaway/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Two Girls and a Blog</a><br /><a href="https://readrantrockandroll.com/2017/04/17/just-around-the-bend-by-renee-paule/#more-3129" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Read, Rant and Rock and Roll</a> - <i>Just Around the Bend</i><br /><a href="https://booksteacupnreviews.wordpress.com/2017/07/09/on-the-other-hand-the-little-anthology-of-big-questions-by-renee-paule/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Books, Teacup and Reviews</a><br /><a href="https://www.bookworks.com/2017/09/first-book-learning-curve-experience/#comment-8387" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">BookWorks</a><br /><a href="https://readrantrockandroll.com/2017/10/02/the-frightened-little-flower-bud-by-renee-paule-and-godfrey-r-hewitt-book-review-and-author-interviews/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Read, Rant and Rock and Roll</a> <i>- The Frightened Little Flower Bud</i><br /><br />Show good will to each other - every day.</span>
